  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_534ede20-fc4a-455e-b378-e90a241a3870'
      });
    }

<a href="/questions/252623-i-am-trying-to-find-a-book-that-my">I am trying to find a book that my grandfather would really like and I know that Vince Flynn is his favorite author. As of right now he just keeps re-reading these books and I know Vince Flynn won&#39;t be coming out with more :(

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I agree- Lee Child's Reacher series is good, David Baldacci's - John Puller series & Camel Club series. For crime series with less military - Michael <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I agree- Lee Child's Reacher series is good, David Baldacci's - John Puller series &amp; Camel Club series. For crime series with less military - Michael Connelly's- Harry Bosch series, Mickey Haller series, William Kent Krueger's - O'Connor series, C.J. Box's- Pickett Series, Steve Hamilton's - McKnight series.... hope he finds any of these enjoyable! I know my Dad has also enjoyed Clive Cussler's books... I haven't gotten to him yet! :) Good luck!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1045118-the-synopsis-is-throwing-me-off-the-pan">The synopsis is throwing me off. The Pan Am Lockerbie attack was in 1988 when the Cold War was ending, not 20 years after. Can I assume the main character is still grieving 20 years after the attack or is this just a poorly thought out timeline that assumes Mr. Flynn&#39;s fan base won&#39;t care he didn&#39;t take the time to get it right?</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8208987-michael">Michael</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Flynn doesn't do a very good job of explaining this, but long story short: this book is a prequel to the rest of the series, which began in 1999. By m<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Flynn doesn't do a very good job of explaining this, but long story short: this book is a prequel to the rest of the series, which began in 1999. By making a few assumptions based on what the book tells us, it takes place in roughly 1990. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13099461521501842876">They need to hire me to proof for them. I’ve come across more than a few books with an unacceptable amount of typos here lately. Is no one reading this stuff before it goes to press?<br/><br/>And I’m not that much of an anal freak, but 20 typos before page 78 is too many.<br/><br/>The reason for my annoyance is because Vince Flynn is a great writer, and I believe I read he is dyslexic, thus he does not have a dedicated team supporting him. That’s a shame because his Mitch Rapp novels tap into the raw emotion of rea</span>
  <span id="freeText13099461521501842876" style="display:none">They need to hire me to proof for them. I’ve come across more than a few books with an unacceptable amount of typos here lately. Is no one reading this stuff before it goes to press?<br /><br />And I’m not that much of an anal freak, but 20 typos before page 78 is too many.<br /><br />The reason for my annoyance is because Vince Flynn is a great writer, and I believe I read he is dyslexic, thus he does not have a dedicated team supporting him. That’s a shame because his Mitch Rapp novels tap into the raw emotion of real America right now, unleashing all our fury against radical Islam.<br /><br />In this 11th novel we meet the man who trained Mitch, the mentor, and he is a fantastic, larger-than-life character. I laughed so hard during his torture scenes with the terrorists. Terrific drama.<br /><br />Vince Flynn reminds us of who we’re supposed to be, and what America is supposed to be about. We’re the best, the baddest, the smartest, the meanest mo-fo on the planet.<br /><br />At least we can still have our fantasies in Vince Flynn’s Mitch Rapp novels.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4307949399666172914">Some people are addicted to drugs. I am happily addicted to Vince Flynn's books and the exploits of his truly American hero, Mitch Rapp. My wife and daughter share my addiction, but they have not had their fix yet because I got to read Flynn's newest book first. Which is only fair since I bought it. My only complaint is that now I will have to wait another year for the next book. Withdrawal can be tough.<br/><br/>Oh, about the book?   <span id="freeText4307949399666172914" style="display:none">Some people are addicted to drugs. I am happily addicted to Vince Flynn's books and the exploits of his truly American hero, Mitch Rapp. My wife and daughter share my addiction, but they have not had their fix yet because I got to read Flynn's newest book first. Which is only fair since I bought it. My only complaint is that now I will have to wait another year for the next book. Withdrawal can be tough.<br /><br />Oh, about the book? C'mon, it's Vince Flynn and Mitch Rapp. This one is about how Mitch got his start in the assassin business before he became the star player in the war on terror and before there was an official war on terror. It is set before 9-11 when some in the clandestine services discerned radical Islamic terror clouds approaching and were trying to prepare for it (remember this is fiction). The result was...Mitch Rapp whose name Islamofacists use to frighten their children with into good behavior when they are not strapping suicide vests on them to kill innocent men women and children. <br /><br />If they ever make a movie based on a Vince Flynn book, this is one I would vote for. That is as long as they were faithful to the book. Otherwise they might tick Vince and Mitch off.</span>

<div id="review_491850593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491850593" />
    <a title="Vijai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14972518-vijai"><img alt="Vijai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388793823p2/14972518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491850593?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vijai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vijai" href="/user/show/14972518-vijai">Vijai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14972518-vijai?shelf=meh">meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491850593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10377608360440898276">Look, here's something about us diehard action-thriller fanboys - we will forgive an author's imprudence with a few weak spots in the plot now and then as long as we get our action-gasm in totality but what we don't do is tolerate preachy one-sided-win story. Two ingredients which this author is dishing out in heaps in this book. <br/><br/>I am not even going to talk about the piss poor editing, its the gross injustice that has been meted out to Mitch Rapp that I am very disappointed with. It took Mr. Fly</span>
  <span id="freeText10377608360440898276" style="display:none">Look, here's something about us diehard action-thriller fanboys - we will forgive an author's imprudence with a few weak spots in the plot now and then as long as we get our action-gasm in totality but what we don't do is tolerate preachy one-sided-win story. Two ingredients which this author is dishing out in heaps in this book. <br /><br />I am not even going to talk about the piss poor editing, its the gross injustice that has been meted out to Mitch Rapp that I am very disappointed with. It took Mr. Flynn exactly three pages to span through Rapp's metamorphosis from a teenager who loses his father to a young adult who loses his first love to become this lethal moral compass all of us have come to love. What? this is Mitch Rapp, the one man army who is that one hope of retribution against the wrong doers, you cannot chalk that up to Irene's exceptional talent hunting skills! all of it justified by making Hurley the bad guy and Stanfield convincing him that he may just have goofed up. NO, you need to take us into the man's head, show us his raw emotions harden into metal and sharpened by balls to the walls kinda training. Instead, what we are shown is that Rapp was an awesome guy all the while. Not to mention the recent trend of brushing a familial touch to justify the loyalty among the characters; Irene thinks of Rapp as her brother, Hurley thinks of Irene as his niece (justifiable by the back-story thankfully provided but come on!) etc., this is not even coming to close Jason Bourne and his son Khan's dismally written about bonding. <br /><br />One of the praises very prominently printed on my copy of this book said something to the effect that Mr.Flynn has an eye on Lee Child's action-thriller throne. The fact that this book is "trying" (very hard) to draw a parallel to Jack Reacher's phenomenal knuckle crunching early-days context story "The Enemy" is not lost on us and I would like to take this opportunity to call FAIL on that. Not with this book, no sir. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10377608360440898276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2036857408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036857408" />
    <a title="* A Reader Obsessed *" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21987508-a-reader-obsessed"><img alt="* A Reader Obsessed *" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524249926p2/21987508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036857408?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="* A Reader Obsessed *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="* A Reader Obsessed *" href="/user/show/21987508-a-reader-obsessed">* A Reader Obsessed *</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21987508-a-reader-obsessed?shelf=z-2017">z-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21987508-a-reader-obsessed?shelf=not-mm">not-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21987508-a-reader-obsessed?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036857408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3067020437617907476"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/> <br/>I’m not gonna lie. The majority of the reason why I started this series was because a certain somebody is starring in the movie version out this September. So as a fangirl, it’s only prudent and necessary to see what this is all about. It’s also not a secret that I love me a military spy action thriller, and with the added bonus of DoB?? That combo is just too hard to resist. <br/> <br/>Depending on what kind of reader you are, you can start with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/184655.Transfer_of_Power__Mitch_Rapp___3_' title='Transfer of Power (Mitch Rapp, #3) by Vince Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Transfer of Power</a>, which was the first book publi</span>
  <span id="freeText3067020437617907476" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /> <br />I’m not gonna lie. The majority of the reason why I started this series was because a certain somebody is starring in the movie version out this September. So as a fangirl, it’s only prudent and necessary to see what this is all about. It’s also not a secret that I love me a military spy action thriller, and with the added bonus of DoB?? That combo is just too hard to resist. <br /> <br />Depending on what kind of reader you are, you can start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/184655.Transfer_of_Power__Mitch_Rapp___3_" title="Transfer of Power (Mitch Rapp, #3) by Vince Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Transfer of Power</a>, which was the first book published, or here, if you’re a chronological purist. This shows the why and how Mitch Rapp becomes the CIA’s most indispensible, top counter-terrorist agent. What begins as a way to deliver retribution to those responsible for the death of his high school sweetheart, turns into something so much more. Rapp is the whole package of well honed athletic talent, no nonsense attitude, nerves of steel, quick thinking and adaptability, coupled with dogged determination and the ability to think way outside the box. Such an autonomous attitude never goes down easily with those way above his pay grade, but it surely is warranted, making Rapp possibly one of the best that the agency’s seen in… well... never. He’s no cookie cutter company man!<br /> <br />So, see how it all begins with this installment. It makes me happy to know there’s many more to go, which means if the movie is successful, we have a great franchise to look forward to! One can only hope!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3067020437617907476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1369579869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369579869" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369579869?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442335233" href="/book/show/9830919-american-assassin">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Political thriller fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matthew by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/12949855-corey">Corey</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=political-thrillers">political-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369579869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8170689866384285068">I have read a couple of the other books in the Mitch Rapp series in the order they were published. Those books came later in the story timeline than American Assassin. When I found out that they published a couple of prequel books, I figured I would go back and give them a try.<br/><br/>American Assassin is just about what you would expect from a political/military/spy thriller. That is not a bad thing! You get all kinds of plotting, action, and badassery. As this is a prequel in the series, it is not in </span>
  <span id="freeText8170689866384285068" style="display:none">I have read a couple of the other books in the Mitch Rapp series in the order they were published. Those books came later in the story timeline than American Assassin. When I found out that they published a couple of prequel books, I figured I would go back and give them a try.<br /><br />American Assassin is just about what you would expect from a political/military/spy thriller. That is not a bad thing! You get all kinds of plotting, action, and badassery. As this is a prequel in the series, it is not in the post 9/11 era, but closer to the fall of the Berlin Wall, the end of the Soviet Union, and the terrorist bombing of the Pan Am flight over Lockerbie, Scotland.<br /><br />A couple things about these types of books that is not a complaint or a praise. Just an observation of two common tropes for this genre:<br /><br />Torture: They really like their torture in these books. The nastier, more uncomfortable, the more painful, the better. So, if you like description of fingernails being ripped out and electrodes being attached to genitals, then this is the genre for you.<br /><br />Confusion: Since deception and undercover work is the name of the game, many times I get lost with these books. Who is on which side? What is the ultimate endgame of the current mission behind enemy lines? Isn't he talking to a guy who just killed his friend in the previous scene but now they are on the same side? It's something I have come to expect and it usually all makes sense in the end.<br /><br />What it comes down to is this: you like this genre, you will like this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8170689866384285068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13507258698740612541">Twenty-three-year-old Mitch Rapp was recruited by Irene Kennedy into a group of highly trained yet clandestine operatives, a division of the CIA. A top athlete, Rapp was incredibly fit and after six months of intense training, he was on his way to his first job in Istanbul. He gave a final thought to the more than two hundred passengers who had lost their lives that day in the Pan Am Lockerbie terrorist attack – retribution was looking good.<br/><br/>As Rapp worked his way across Europe, he finally found </span>
  <span id="freeText13507258698740612541" style="display:none">Twenty-three-year-old Mitch Rapp was recruited by Irene Kennedy into a group of highly trained yet clandestine operatives, a division of the CIA. A top athlete, Rapp was incredibly fit and after six months of intense training, he was on his way to his first job in Istanbul. He gave a final thought to the more than two hundred passengers who had lost their lives that day in the Pan Am Lockerbie terrorist attack – retribution was looking good.<br /><br />As Rapp worked his way across Europe, he finally found himself in Beirut on a mission of recovery. But would it all go wrong? Would he find himself in the hands of the terrorists himself? The skills he had learned; the devious nature of the hunt – could he survive and achieve his goal? Mitch Rapp was the new kid on the block…<br /><br /><i>American Assassin</i> is the first in the Mitch Rapp series by Vince Flynn and I enjoyed it very much. Fast paced, intense and chilling, this spy thriller has plenty of twists and turns, loads of action, and a hero who is worth reading about. Highly recommended.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1963364825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963364825" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24668886-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381636198p2/24668886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963364825?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/24668886-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24668886-scott?shelf=books-read-but-not-owned">books-read-but-not-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963364825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15799622697745706328">Let me start with a couple of important points before I get knee deep in my review. First, this is my first time reading a Vince Flynn “Mitch Rapp” book. I have a friend who enjoys reading Lee Child’s “Reacher” series like I do, and he recommended this series to me. Second, I understand there was a less than stellar editing work done on this book in the series as noted in several of the Goodreads reviews I read online. I agree with these points, but am moving past them.<br/><br/>Now for my review… Wow! I </span>
  <span id="freeText15799622697745706328" style="display:none">Let me start with a couple of important points before I get knee deep in my review. First, this is my first time reading a Vince Flynn “Mitch Rapp” book. I have a friend who enjoys reading Lee Child’s “Reacher” series like I do, and he recommended this series to me. Second, I understand there was a less than stellar editing work done on this book in the series as noted in several of the Goodreads reviews I read online. I agree with these points, but am moving past them.<br /><br />Now for my review… Wow! I was pleasantly surprised. To be honest, I think that I was expecting a hardcore military hero that was invincible and boring. Well, that is not the case. It must be noted that this is not the first book written in the series, but part of two prequel books that help explain the main character, Mitch Rapp’s, evolution into the strong character he is in the other books. I chose to start here so I could see his beginning. And what a beginning he has… Mitch Rapp gets recruited into an “off book” group of American assassins who help the U.S. government do what it cannot openly admit to publicly. This includes meeting his trainer and mentor, his first mission, and the set-up of his organizational team during the growth of terrorism in the middle east.<br /><br />Why did I like the book? The characters, plotting, and fast moving intertwining plot lines that come together at the end were all strong points of the book. The establishment of the aging and experienced Hurley as Rapp’s trainer and mentor was one the most interesting things in the book. Hurley’s character stole the show at times and demanded the reader’s attention. Rapp’s growth and development in his first couple of missions was engrossing and tough to stop reading. There were some preachy moments, but the three-pronged - American / terrorist jihad / Russian - storylines built well and came to an exciting and tension filled climax.<br /><br />Overall, I was really surprised at how much I enjoyed this first Mitch Rapp adventure. So much so, I immediately bought the second prequel book, “Kill Shot” on my Amazon Kindle. I love reading suspense and thriller authors like Lee Child and David Baldacci, and am now adding Vince Flynn to my list. If you haven’t, maybe you should give Flynn’s “Mitch Rapp” a try too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15799622697745706328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1765911438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1765911438" />
    <a title="Hiroto" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30110759-hiroto"><img alt="Hiroto" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414052104p2/30110759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765911438?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hiroto" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hiroto" href="/user/show/30110759-hiroto">Hiroto</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=failed-character-development">failed-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=babbled">babbled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=not-my-division">not-my-division</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=dylan-made-me-read-it">dylan-made-me-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30110759-hiroto?shelf=give-me-a-big-red-pen">give-me-a-big-red-pen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1765911438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7710001665512052773">Oh Dylan, Dylan, Dylan my good dude why.<br/><br/>Where do I start? The character development is piss poor. So our good Mitch Rapp (wtf is this name? it sounds so dumb??) lost his father at 13yo because of a heart attack and his highschool sweetheart in a terrorist attack so he's super familiar with death (ok?) and his heart is bursting with REVENGE. Coincidentally he's picked out by Langlsey wich is like a branch of the CIA, even thought he didn't do antyhing to be noticed (ok??) and he's sent off to a s</span>
  <span id="freeText7710001665512052773" style="display:none">Oh Dylan, Dylan, Dylan my good dude why.<br /><br />Where do I start? The character development is piss poor. So our good Mitch Rapp (wtf is this name? it sounds so dumb??) lost his father at 13yo because of a heart attack and his highschool sweetheart in a terrorist attack so he's super familiar with death (ok?) and his heart is bursting with REVENGE. Coincidentally he's picked out by Langlsey wich is like a branch of the CIA, even thought he didn't do antyhing to be noticed (ok??) and he's sent off to a six-months training of the death where he excells at everything and learns super fast because he's an athlete you know, he was super good at lacrosse in highschool and he can run at the speed of the light (ok????) and then wooish he's sent to Beirut to do his first kill (ok???????).<br />Really.<br /><br />Though it has to be noted that the book actually follow 4 POVs : the russian's, switching between Ivankov and his subaltern, the Libyan's with Sayyed (who's the most developped I think, the character was gimmicky but not outrigh cliché), and two Americans : Mitch Rapp's- pfffrh that name- and Hursley's. The latter is the most dumb and grossly written character of the book, but he's entertaining (like, at the end of his very first POV, we learn that he pisses in the bush of his very cool estate. ok? I don't give a damn? I don't know what that adds to the story, and that actually doesn't say a lot about this character). I think it says a lot when I thought Mitch Rapp's -honhonhon- POV was the most boring to me.<br /><br />There's one thing the book does right I think : a lot of the usually faceless muslims villains are actually <i>named</i>, and we do follow them a good chunk of the book. So if the upcoming film (why did you think I read this book in the first place) follows the same pace and story, maybe we'll have actors with names and talent playing them, and they'll have screentime, and wouldn't that be a nice change ?<br />Thought I read somewhere they cast a turkish actress I think, and I have no idea what her role will be, since the only two named female characters of this book are both white and blonde.<br /><br />The writing isn't that great either, I did spot typos and a lot of phrases like "you’d expect from someone who was expected to", this book wasn't edited properly. Also I could have started a new drinking game where I take a shot every time the words "trained/training" appeared (spoiler : a lot). There were a lot of gimmicky phrase such as "million years of survival instincts embedded into the human brain like gene".<br /><br />Annnnd the two main things I didn't like about it : this book was very, and I mean very, black &amp; white, bad guys vs. good guys (there's even a character saying this exact phrase "well, let's just say I believe in good guys and bad guys" wow). The second point is : the author's opinions is always interfering in the book, like "he saw communism for the sham it was" or a phrase about stupid people covering their women with sheets (funny reading that in a book where the word "pussy" is written a least 6 times, talk about sexism ahahah).<br />Now, i haven't read a lot of books of this gendra. Maybe it's the norm, it's suppposed to make the americans readers feel like the baddest mofo in the planet. As an europpean one though, it felt laughable and super cliché, we always make fun of this type of movies where the white dude is super badass and kill everything. That's why I giggled in the more ridiculous parts.<br /><br />I won't mention the plotholes because, welp, but I will add that there weren't even that much of action. I expected to feel at least some tension, but I wasn't pumped up in the slightest.<br /><br />So yeah, Dylan, I hope the script is better than this, I keep imagining something à la "The Raid" like the whole film is about the rescue mission (but it's only like ~20pages in the book). I don't understand why you'd sign another franchise, but you know, good luck my dude, have fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7710001665512052773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_141186022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141186022" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2047287-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447364748p2/2047287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141186022?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/2047287-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9338193-american-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141186022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6048137345840227158">This was exceptional with one disclaimer... it was obviously rushed to publishing with little editing. While waiting for my copy to arrive I read that other fans had noticed more than the occasional typos in the text and were bothered by them. I wondered if perhaps they were being a little over the top. Unfortunately, I found myself equally bothered. It is understandable that sometimes a "i" will be replaced with an "l" (as in the word "cabbie" being written as "cabble" in the last portion of th</span>
  <span id="freeText6048137345840227158" style="display:none">This was exceptional with one disclaimer... it was obviously rushed to publishing with little editing. While waiting for my copy to arrive I read that other fans had noticed more than the occasional typos in the text and were bothered by them. I wondered if perhaps they were being a little over the top. Unfortunately, I found myself equally bothered. It is understandable that sometimes a "i" will be replaced with an "l" (as in the word "cabbie" being written as "cabble" in the last portion of the book) but in one area an entire name was substituted with the name of a different primary character who was most certainly not present in the room - this kind of error attacked the rhythm and flow of the book and distracted me on too many occasions. It is a shame that such a great story was marred by so many glaring errors.<br /><br />I saw the interview with Vince Flynn after the release of the book and remembered him saying that in this prequel even he "learned things about Mitch Rapp" that he did not previously know. I was struck, while reading, about how true that is. Rapp is a great character who has always been easy to root for. This book only furthers my affection for him and my desire to know him more. <br /><br />The end of the book left a number of things teased or unanswered leaving me wondering if there are more prequels to come. <br /><br />Without question I enjoyed the story, was angry and unnerved by the realistic implications of the plot and my gratitude for real American Black Ops was furthered. While reading this I cannot help but think of Winston Churchill's famous quote: "never was so much owed by so many to so few." <br /><br />Between Tom Clancy, Vince Flynn, The Unit and 24, I do hope that our culture will embrace the ugly reality that the face of war has changed and what we hold most dear is not nearly as safe as we would hope. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6048137345840227158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6828301159636163281">This has been on my TBR list for a long time, I had been reluctant to read it as there are so many comparisons to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5091.Lee_Child' title='Lee Child' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lee Child</a> that I expected to be disappointed.   <span id="freeText6828301159636163281" style="display:none">This has been on my TBR list for a long time, I had been reluctant to read it as there are so many comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5091.Lee_Child" title="Lee Child" rel="nofollow noopener">Lee Child</a> that I expected to be disappointed. However, I can now see why the comparisons have been made as this was just as good! <br />As with Reacher we have a hero that is the complete package. Smart, strong and not too arrogant. The story unfolded beautifully but was violent and described a lot of torture (best to avoid if you find this off putting). I will definitely be continuing with this series! Highly recommended.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185653000" />
    <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw"><img alt="Doug Bradshaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548429066p2/808994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185653000?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Bradshaw" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw">Doug Bradshaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185653000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14233825091576939878">This is good tough American male stuff. I enjoyed as much as some of you women readers enjoy a romance novel with handsome vampires and whatnot. It made me almost laugh to read it, like going back in time to the joy of reading my first three or four Ludlum novels. <br/><br/>This is the 11th book in a series about a CIA assassin named Mitch Rapp. It is the prequel to the other already told stories and I was told I may as well read it first. It's not quite as sophisticated as Jack Bauer and "24", but it has</span>
  <span id="freeText14233825091576939878" style="display:none">This is good tough American male stuff. I enjoyed as much as some of you women readers enjoy a romance novel with handsome vampires and whatnot. It made me almost laugh to read it, like going back in time to the joy of reading my first three or four Ludlum novels. <br /><br />This is the 11th book in a series about a CIA assassin named Mitch Rapp. It is the prequel to the other already told stories and I was told I may as well read it first. It's not quite as sophisticated as Jack Bauer and "24", but it has that same tough agent willing to do what it takes even if it means ignoring the more politically correct bosses, attitude. Here is a simple, likable, extremely tough athletic guy willing to sacrifice his limbs and life to beat the terrorists. The toughest and most pure quarterback you'll ever meet. And he's able, as a young guy, to show the leaders at the top how it needs to be done and how they have strayed from their real missions and directives by being too politically correct.<br /><br />Sort of like the warnings the drug companies have to give us on TV, there is extreme violence, graphic killing, the toughest, worst, sob drill sergeant ever, a little romance but nothing you women will enjoy, and other such fun and games.<br /><br />I loved it and will now go to the first in the series. <br /><br />I'd give it five stars, but I'm afraid some of my old English Professors may be reading this and, the book certainly isn't literature. But it is efficient, has some great moments and will give you a vicarious thrill here and there, although, sometimes, perhaps, a little over the top. But I'd never cut anything out if I were the editor. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14233825091576939878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_384513174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384513174" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7932604-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330271616p2/7932604.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384513174?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/7932604-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384513174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4188820844385722387">I was curious about the Vince Flynn series featuring Mitch Rapp since the books do well on the NY Times Bestseller list and I like thrillers. I was less than thrilled to see endorsements by folks of the Glenn Beck ilk. Nevertheless, I read this book, and likened it to a "less well-written-than-the-Bourne-series" book. In other words, I prefer the writing of Robert Ludlum. This is a spy versus spy story, with the requisite close calls, seemingly impossible dilemmas, and shoot-outs. A bit too much</span>
  <span id="freeText4188820844385722387" style="display:none">I was curious about the Vince Flynn series featuring Mitch Rapp since the books do well on the NY Times Bestseller list and I like thrillers. I was less than thrilled to see endorsements by folks of the Glenn Beck ilk. Nevertheless, I read this book, and likened it to a "less well-written-than-the-Bourne-series" book. In other words, I prefer the writing of Robert Ludlum. This is a spy versus spy story, with the requisite close calls, seemingly impossible dilemmas, and shoot-outs. A bit too much torture for me, and I think the characters are two-dimensional. I also didn't like the fact that virtually all the Russians and Arabs are super-evil and all the Americans are the white-hat guys and gals. Stereotypes and nationalism are to be expected, but I would have found this book to be better if the characters and cultures weren't portrayed in such a cardboard manner. That being said, it did pass the time and was mildly entertaining. I hear that this book is the basis of an upcoming film. I hope the film avoids such broad sweeps.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4188820844385722387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8482387912072741730">Ok, how in the world have I missed this author, these characters, these books?! I think I may have teared up a little, but if not an actual tear, I at least danced. At the risk of oversimplifying... this book rocked!   <span id="freeText8482387912072741730" style="display:none">Ok, how in the world have I missed this author, these characters, these books?! You know that feeling you get when you realize you found a new (to you) outstanding author and he/she has piles of books you have not yet read? I think I may have teared up a little, but if not an actual tear, I at least danced. At the risk of oversimplifying... this book rocked! It reminded me a bit of a Lee Child book where the main character is still affiliated with the military. Great characters, deep courage and non-stop action.<br /><br />I cannot wait to read the next in this series!</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2429924528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4825428457800963495">#1 in the Mitch Rapp Series.<br/>This book was first published in 2010 and 8 years later it is to be released as a movie.<br/>I can see why producers would turn this into a movie as it is one heart pumping adrenalin rush from page one onwards.<br/>Mitch Rapp is one young man with a huge chip on his shoulders that verges on a death wish. Mitch lost the love of his life in a cruel, mindless act of terrorism. In the book it was the bombing of Pan AM flight 103 in Lockerbie Scotland. The movie no doubt will be dif</span>
  <span id="freeText4825428457800963495" style="display:none">#1 in the Mitch Rapp Series.<br />This book was first published in 2010 and 8 years later it is to be released as a movie.<br />I can see why producers would turn this into a movie as it is one heart pumping adrenalin rush from page one onwards.<br />Mitch Rapp is one young man with a huge chip on his shoulders that verges on a death wish. Mitch lost the love of his life in a cruel, mindless act of terrorism. In the book it was the bombing of Pan AM flight 103 in Lockerbie Scotland. The movie no doubt will be different.<br />Mitch now lives for one purpose and one purpose only to take revenge on the people who perpetrated this unspeakable act.<br />Mitch comes to the attention of Irene Kennedy a top of the line recruitment officers for the CIA.<br />When Director Kennedy tells Mitch what she has in mind Mitch starts salivating. Six months of intensive training and Mitch is ready to be released on an unsuspecting terrorist world.<br />By the time the terrorists know what has happened they have lost millions in funds. The factions start blaming each other of stealing the money. High placed agents are turning up dead. The terrorists are being terrorised.<br /><br />The pace is frenetic. The tension is nail bitting and a lot of Zealots get a quick passage to paradise. <br /><br />Recommended if you like your reading with more than a touch of violence. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4825428457800963495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14633211775556862314">Review of the audiobook narrated by George Guidall.<br/><br/>I'm impressed. I've watched plenty of spy thriller movies, but this was my first novel in the genre. I was expecting dumbed-down action with one dimensional characters and that was not at all what I got. Mitch Rapp is intriguing, exciting and likable, yet has some real flaws. Hurley is a bad-ass, I loved that character.   <span id="freeText14633211775556862314" style="display:none">Review of the audiobook narrated by George Guidall.<br /><br />I'm impressed. I've watched plenty of spy thriller movies, but this was my first novel in the genre. I was expecting dumbed-down action with one dimensional characters and that was not at all what I got. Mitch Rapp is intriguing, exciting and likable, yet has some real flaws. Hurley is a bad-ass, I loved that character. Flynn narrowing avoids making the bad guys too cliche and we are left with a fast moving plot with a great pay-off. <br /><br />I wasn't aware that this was written as a prequel until afterwards. It is meant to be read first in the series though. I'll definitely be reading more of this series!<br /><br />George Guidall provides an impressive narration. I understand now why he's in Audible's Narrator Hall of Fame. Looking forward in the series I see he is not the narrator of books 3-5 so that may be a tough decision to skip them or not once I get there.<br /><br />Final verdict: 5 star story, 5 star narration, 5 stars overall</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1344223487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12916504773017800360">American Assassin is definitely an addition to the spy thriller genre. It felt fresh and relevant in 2018. Rapp is an interesting character. I appreciate the drive for vengeance (something many wanted after 9/11). I also enjoyed that he isn’t your typical, former military man turned spy. The only drawback is the climax and resolution felt hurried. I also feel like the love interest plot line is a little James Bond. Overall, it was an enjoyable, fast-paced read that never failed to entertain.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2084515188" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084515188" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3308557-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560181081p2/3308557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2084515188?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/3308557-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36096550-american-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3308557-summer?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3308557-summer?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3308557-summer?shelf=series-dnf">series-dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084515188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18260666426146711467">Hoo boy. First things first: If you're interested in reading this because of the upcoming film, you'll likely be disappointed. The plot of this book and the plot of the movie seem completely different, with the only similarity being the presence of the main character. <br/><br/>Now the book itself is pretty much a handbook on toxic masculinity. It starts out pretty spectacularly, with the author likening a lack of honor to "emasculat[ion]" and "questioning the size of [one's] balls for as long as [one] li</span>
  <span id="freeText18260666426146711467" style="display:none">Hoo boy. First things first: If you're interested in reading this because of the upcoming film, you'll likely be disappointed. The plot of this book and the plot of the movie seem completely different, with the only similarity being the presence of the main character. <br /><br />Now the book itself is pretty much a handbook on toxic masculinity. It starts out pretty spectacularly, with the author likening a lack of honor to "emasculat[ion]" and "questioning the size of [one's] balls for as long as [one] lived" in the prologue. From there, it's basically a fever dream of wish fulfillment. Rapp goes from living with his mother to an "efficient, badass killing machine" in six months, without any prior military training. He becomes an expert marksman, learns several languages, and becomes an expert at hand-to-hand combat after a few months in - I'm not even kidding - a strip mall dojo. He understands that a civilized society is weak, the media is working against the country's safety, and emotions are bad. <br /><br />Well, except when they're not. Rapp's transition into a lethal operative is built on the grief resulting from his girlfriend's death. His love for her is portrayed as something incredibly meaningful, given that his life revolves around killing people to avenge her death. That is, until a stereotypical blonde beauty appears in the narrative, at which point he can't wait to get her into bed and move on from his girlfriend. Grief and vengeance seem to be the only acceptable emotions in this world, as his mentor's grief own grief causes him to "go running off half-cocked killing whomever he wanted." And that's another weakness in the plot: this team of elite, highly-trained, infallible super soldiers do some epically stupid things that would surely get them killed by their own superiors if this world had any internal consistency. <br /><br />And, of course, there's your smattering of casual misogyny: calling men ladies and pussies as motivational insults and the good guys sleeping with sex-trafficked prostitutes. And my favorite gem: "You piss and moan like some miserable woman who's mad at her husband because she's no longer young and beautiful."<br /><br />Plus, there are issues of repetitive writing and poor pacing. All in all, I'm going to take my "PC bullshit" and read other authors whose writing doesn't make me roll me eyes so hard I feel like I'm going to break something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18260666426146711467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144093393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144093393" />
    <a title="Chuck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84112-chuck"><img alt="Chuck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442475386p2/84112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144093393?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chuck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chuck" href="/user/show/84112-chuck">Chuck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144093393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11567601686201038512">Although I don't think many people actually follow what I say, I have to retract the criticism I made of Flynn's last few books. Actually, I'm not going to retract them, because they were true--Flynn was letting his ideology get in the way of the storytelling. Rather, I will say that he's returned to the stuff that made his earlier work great--compelling characters, amazing story lines, and a breathtaking adventure that leaves you sorry when the book ends.<br/><br/>Flynn takes his hero, Mitch Rapp, back t</span>
  <span id="freeText11567601686201038512" style="display:none">Although I don't think many people actually follow what I say, I have to retract the criticism I made of Flynn's last few books. Actually, I'm not going to retract them, because they were true--Flynn was letting his ideology get in the way of the storytelling. Rather, I will say that he's returned to the stuff that made his earlier work great--compelling characters, amazing story lines, and a breathtaking adventure that leaves you sorry when the book ends.<br /><br />Flynn takes his hero, Mitch Rapp, back to the beginning, when he is a 23 year old who's just lost the love of his life to tragedy. Mitch's reasons for becoming who we know him to be--the American Assassin--are compelling and believable. There's also some interesting moral analysis between the idea of revenge and retribution. We also get to see other characters from the series younger, and, in the case of Thomas Stansfield, still alive.<br /><br />If you like the Mitch Rapp series, you'll adore this book. If you've never read a Mitch Rapp novel, this is a terrific place to start.<br /><br />Well done, Mr. Flynn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11567601686201038512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_603138897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/603138897" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3077040-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483660268p2/3077040.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/603138897?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/3077040-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3077040-jo?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603138897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12221320974946328371">American Assassin <br/>By Vince Flynn<br/>Genre-Thriller<br/>Two decades after the Cold War, Islamic terrorism is on the rise, and CIA Operations Director Thomas Stansfield forms a new group of clandestine operatives—men who do not exist—to meet this burgeoning threat abroad, before it reaches America’s shores. Stansfield’s protégé, Irene Kennedy, finds the ideal candidate in the wake of the Pan Am Lockerbie terrorist attack. Among the thousands grieving the victims is Mitch Rapp, a gifted college athlete, who</span>
  <span id="freeText12221320974946328371" style="display:none">American Assassin <br />By Vince Flynn<br />Genre-Thriller<br />Two decades after the Cold War, Islamic terrorism is on the rise, and CIA Operations Director Thomas Stansfield forms a new group of clandestine operatives—men who do not exist—to meet this burgeoning threat abroad, before it reaches America’s shores. Stansfield’s protégé, Irene Kennedy, finds the ideal candidate in the wake of the Pan Am Lockerbie terrorist attack. Among the thousands grieving the victims is Mitch Rapp, a gifted college athlete, who wants only one thing: retribution. Six months of intense training prepare him to devastate the enemy with brutal efficiency, leaving a trail of bodies from Istanbul and across Europe, to Beirut. But there, the American assassin will need every ounce of skill and cunning to survive the war-ravaged city and its deadly terrorist faction<br /><br />Review<br />This is Vince Flynn's eleventh Mitch Rapp thriller and is a prequel to the series.Vince Flynn is one of my favorite authors, while others are singing the praises of Lee Child, I prefer Vince Flynn and Daniel Silva. Both of these authors write thrillers that are consistently good, there are no flops unlike Mr Child. American Assassin is set at the very beginning of Mitch Rapp's death-defying career. It places him in the aftermath of the event that forever changed his life. The 1988 Lockerbie Pan Am Flight 103 bombing that killed 270 people, including the one woman he loved. Recruited into joining the CIA, Rapp is placed in an intense, fast track training program and then assigned to a clandestine group of covert ops assigned to permanently neutralize the terrorists. His fearless search for vengeance leads him into the very dens of the Middle East conspirators.<br /><br />For those looking for a great series for the males in their life this is it. Vince Flynn's Mitch Rapp series is an adrenaline-fueled, action-packed thriller that doesn't disappoint.<br />5 stars <br />Reread as my last book for 2019. Wanted to end my reading challenge with a book I loved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12221320974946328371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1002182185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002182185" />
    <a title="Gloria ~ mzglorybe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1066448-gloria-mzglorybe"><img alt="Gloria ~ mzglorybe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553573460p2/1066448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002182185?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gloria ~ mzglorybe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gloria ~ mzglorybe" href="/user/show/1066448-gloria-mzglorybe">Gloria ~ mzglorybe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002182185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15686235121094808290">If you want to start the Mitch Rapp series, start here. Do NOT pass this series up if you are a fan of this genre. This is the best political espionage/military series we've (family members) ever read. After Book #1 the rest of the novels are fast-paced, edge of your seat, very hard to put down. This first book gives the reader a glance at what the protagonist was like in his youth, in this case, prior to Rapp's recruitment into this covert mercenary group right out of college. <br/><br/>The first half of</span>
  <span id="freeText15686235121094808290" style="display:none">If you want to start the Mitch Rapp series, start here. Do NOT pass this series up if you are a fan of this genre. This is the best political espionage/military series we've (family members) ever read. After Book #1 the rest of the novels are fast-paced, edge of your seat, very hard to put down. This first book gives the reader a glance at what the protagonist was like in his youth, in this case, prior to Rapp's recruitment into this covert mercenary group right out of college. <br /><br />The first half of this book was all about the people who recruited Rapp and why, and all about his training. The bickering between them tedious at times and the training, yeah, we get it, it was hard. Be patient... It really got interesting after he actually got into assignments and his missions in the Middle East. Remember this is pre-911, but after the Pan-Am Lockerbie disaster of 1988. Most of his writing references true facts, with exception of the fictional characters.<br /><br />My family and I are fans of the Reacher series by Lee Child, and the Baldacci novels of political espionage. We are happy to have another series to follow as we are caught up with the others. We were turned onto Vince Flynn by another reviewer who stated that Baldacci's writing of "The Target" (which we loved, btw) reminded him of Flynn's Mitch Rapp series. We had not heard of Vince Flynn at the time, so we started with this one. Boy are we glad we did. It gave us months of intense suspense and reading enjoyment in a realistic setting what with all that is going on in the world. We read all the books he wrote in this series prior to his untimely death, and grieved right along with everyone else when it happened :(<br /><br />If you decide to read this, be patient the first half, it gets intense in the second half and it is not a large book as some of his later books are. Most of the novels after this one in the series earned 5 well-deserved stars from us. I still miss Vince Flynn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15686235121094808290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V+KmpjR4xSNywpteQIuJwITUwDeJ6u4zDfSRAGECF61jFY4mjKTPVbgPu6U7LQivjPvT3Dp7O+WxVejks+skCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0uMqWUUZ/ehM8f9iypDli7R4sPuIhDx0B8jOuZ2e7gTmFALZ/cX3noY835mxNmTkvFejEDsV6aK7abddT3fdoA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9036491696462635634">The fifth of seven children, Vince Flynn was born in St. Paul, Minnesota, in 1966. He graduated from the St. Thomas Academy in 1984, and the University of St. Thomas with a degree in economics in 1988.<br/><br/>After college he went to work for Kraft General Foods where he was an account and sales marketing specialist. In 1990 he left Kraft to accept an aviation candidate slot with the United States Marine </span>
  <span id="freeText9036491696462635634" style="display:none">The fifth of seven children, Vince Flynn was born in St. Paul, Minnesota, in 1966. He graduated from the St. Thomas Academy in 1984, and the University of St. Thomas with a degree in economics in 1988.<br /><br />After college he went to work for Kraft General Foods where he was an account and sales marketing specialist. In 1990 he left Kraft to accept an aviation candidate slot with the United States Marine Corps. One week before leaving for Officers Candidate School, he was medically disqualified from the Marine Aviation Program, due to several concussions and convulsive seizures he suffered growing up. While trying to obtain a medical waiver for his condition, he started thinking about writing a book. This was a very unusual choice for Flynn since he had been diagnosed with dyslexia in grade school and had struggled with reading and writing all his life.<br /><br />Having been stymied by the Marine Corps, Flynn returned to the nine-to-five grind and took a job with United Properties, a commercial real estate company in the Twin Cities. During his spare time he worked on an idea he had for a book. After two years with United Properties he decided to take a big gamble. He quit his job, moved to Colorado, and began working full time on what would eventually become Term Limits.<br /><br />Like many struggling artists before him, he bartended at night and wrote during the day. Five years and more than sixty rejection letters later he took the unusual step of self-publishing his first novel. The book went to number one in the Twin Cities, and within a week had a new agent and two-book deal with Pocket Books, a Simon &amp; Schuster imprint. <br /><br />Vince Flynn passed away on June 19, 2013 after a three year battle with prostate cancer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9036491696462635634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
